GitHub Copilot: I’m re-checking the exact seam now that the question is narrower: whether the matrix builder is actually aligned with the IAEL consumer, or whether they’re speaking different canonical schemas.

Read [](file:///c%3A/Users/rick/projects/Atlas/src/Atlas/engine/new_probability.py#1-1), lines 1 to 160

Read [](file:///c%3A/Users/rick/projects/Atlas/src/Atlas/engine/new_probability.py#620-620), lines 620 to 760

Read [](file:///c%3A/Users/rick/projects/Atlas/tools/build_share_matrix.py)

Yes, but I’d call it a pipeline mismatch more than a matrix-schema mismatch.

What I see:

- build_share_matrix.py does an IAEL refresh as a side effect, then builds the matrix only from `nba_gamelogs.csv` via team_share_reallocator.py. It does not actually consume IAEL rows when deriving weights.
- The runtime consumer in new_probability.py loads IAEL from `status_latest.json` and only applies the share matrix if IAEL is present. If IAEL is missing, the path falls back to `no_iael` and the matrix is effectively bypassed.
- So the builder and the runtime are not looking at the same kind of evidence. The builder is historical rotation/absence inference from gamelogs; the runtime is current IAEL-based outs matching.
- There is also a normalization mismatch risk:
  - iael_filter.py uses order-insensitive token sorting for IAEL name matching.
  - new_probability.py uses a different canonicalizer.
  - team_share_reallocator.py has yet another internal name key path.
  - Those are close enough for common names, but they are not identical, so edge-case joins can fail.
- The matrix schema itself does line up reasonably well with runtime expectations: `team`, `out_player`, `beneficiary_player`, `stat`, `games`, `weight`.

So my answer is:

- No, I don’t think the primary problem is a bad CSV schema.
- Yes, I do think there is a mismatch between IAEL and the share-matrix build/runtime contract:
  - build-time evidence source is gamelog-derived
  - run-time evidence source is IAEL-derived
  - normalization logic is not unified
  - missing/stale IAEL makes the runtime act like the matrix is absent

That matches the `no_iael` behavior we saw in the last replay run.

If you want, I can next do one of these:
1. Trace the exact name-normalization path for Julius Randle and Anthony Edwards to prove whether they join cleanly end-to-end.
2. Suggest a concrete unification patch so builder and runtime share the same canonical IAEL/player key function.

Yes. The allocator has several real calibration levers, and the safest way to improve Brier or legloss is usually to make it less aggressive, not more aggressive.

The highest-impact places in team_share_reallocator.py are:

- team_share_reallocator.py, because Q statuses currently count as 0.5 out. If those tags are noisy, this can inflate removed budget and hurt calibration.
- team_share_reallocator.py, because sparse share patterns get influence too early. Raising this makes the allocator wait for stronger evidence.
- team_share_reallocator.py, because weakly supported patterns still get a large fraction of the redistribution budget. Lowering this is a direct way to reduce overconfidence.
- team_share_reallocator.py and the guardrail caps in team_share_reallocator.py, because they control tail inflation. Tightening them often helps Brier and legloss if the model is too “hot”.
- team_share_reallocator.py through team_share_reallocator.py, because it determines how much removed production gets reallocated at all.

What I would not change first:

- team_share_reallocator.py is already conservative at 0.2, so it is probably not the main problem.
- team_share_reallocator.py mostly affects builder smoothing, not the immediate runtime calibration signal.

The important read is this: if the gate failures are from overprediction or overconfidence, tighten the allocator. If they are from underprediction, you would do the opposite. So the right direction depends on whether your backtest is showing positive or negative error bias.

My practical recommendation for a first calibration pass is:

- lower team_share_reallocator.py
- raise team_share_reallocator.py
- lower team_share_reallocator.py
- tighten team_share_reallocator.py and the guardrail caps in team_share_reallocator.py

That is the part of the code that is most likely to move Brier and legloss in the right direction for reader gates.

If you want, I can make a conservative calibration patch now and tune those defaults downward in a controlled way.

- The worst errors are a mix of extreme underpredictions on hits and overconfident misses, especially on combo props.

What to tighten next:
- First priority: increase role-context coverage. The fact that `no_outs` dominates means the allocator is often not contributing enough signal to move the reader.
- Second priority: tighten combo-stat handling. `PRA` and `RA` are the weakest buckets, and the largest misses are concentrated there.
- Third priority: reduce or retrain the calibration map, because `p_cal` is only marginally better than `p_adj`, which suggests the current calibration layer is not giving you much lift.

Bottom line:
- The replay passed.
- It is not obviously gate-ready yet.
- The next practical lever is not more brute-force allocator aggression; it is better coverage plus combo-stat calibration cleanup.
